Education News

Outside this Locale

Two Subjects Failed in the Joint Examination

Allowed to Retake the Exam Twice

Instruction from the Ministry of Education to the Beijing Municipal Social Affairs Bureau

The Ministry of Education, based on a report from the Nanjing Municipal Social Affairs Bureau regarding the completion of the first semester's joint high school graduation examination for the 22nd year in this city, and concerning whether students who failed one or two subjects in the previous joint examination and still failed the make-up examination this time can be allowed to retake the examination again, issued an instruction to the bureau stating that students who failed one or two subjects in the joint examination are temporarily allowed to participate in the next examination for each of the failed subjects twice. If these students still fail the subjects in this high school graduation joint examination in this city, they should be allowed to retake the examination once more in the next joint examination. Please take note immediately.

The Jiangsu Province Middle School Military Training Student Team Holds General Review

A Total of Twenty-Three Schools and One Thousand Three Hundred and Seventy-Seven People Arrived

The General Review Officer Zhu Sends Zhang Huafu as Representative

The Field Exercise is Changed to be Held Outside the East Gate

(Zhenjiang Express News) The Jiangsu Provincial National Military Training Committee, taking advantage of the school spring break period, specially held the Jiangsu Province Secondary School Business Middle School Grade Student Spring Break Grand Exercise. The general review was held at the county stadium at 8 o'clock yesterday morning. As of 6 o'clock last night, a total of twenty-three schools, with a total of one thousand three hundred and seventy-seven people, had reported and set up camp in the provincial and county stadiums. The details are recorded below:

General Review Officer: Hu Dun, Director of the Jiangsu National Military Training Committee, had previously telegraphed Zhu Peide, Director of Training, to serve as the General Review Officer. He has now received a reply telegram from Zhu stating that he cannot come to Zhenjiang due to official business, and has sent Deputy Director Zhang Huafu as a representative. It is reported that Zhang has already arrived in Zhenjiang yesterday. The other judges hired, Gao Hefei, Luo Zhuohan, Jiang Xuhai, Zhang Lianfen, Hou Zhiqing, Yuan Ying, Lai Zhongwei, Cheng Jihou, Yuan Qishou, and Wang Jingxi, are all current officials from the General Supervision Department's Security Office Military Training Institute and other places, and are well-versed in military knowledge.

Review Ceremony: According to Director Hu, the purpose of holding this exercise is to enhance the students' martial spirit, to integrate soldiers into agriculture, and to integrate generals into learning. It only seeks to invigorate the students' spirit and to make their movements orderly, just like a normal military review. Therefore, the ceremony is not elaborate. Only the General Review Officer gives a speech before the review begins. The layout in front of the reviewing stand is also extremely simple, with only a white cloth banner hung on the reviewing stand, reading "General Review of Jiangsu Military Training Students Spring Break, 23rd Year of the Republic of China". The couplets on both sides are "Strengthening the nation is about combining literacy and martial arts, and military training cultivates a fearless spirit". A portrait of the Premier is hung in the middle, and slogans are pasted all around.

Number of People Reporting: The original plan was for twenty-five schools to participate, but because the instructor of the Yan and Cuiying schools, Huang Xianli, requested leave due to illness and could not participate, the actual number of schools was twenty-three, with a total of one thousand three hundred and seventy-seven people. In addition, Private Xichang School was not listed, but it has already reported yesterday. Whether it will formally participate is still being considered by the Military Training Committee. The names of the reporting schools, the number of people, and the names of the instructors are recorded below:

Jiangnan District Schools: Shangzhong, number of people 103, instructor's name Jia Jianping; Su Gong Zhuan, 37, Wang Yixuan; Suzhou Middle School, 97, Wang Yixuan; Su Nong, 35, Huang Xianli; Changzhou Middle School, 75 Chen Diping; Nanjing Middle School, 146, He Jichang; Zhenjiang Normal School, 61, Tang Yuanli; Taicang Normal School, 50, Zeng Weigong; Xixi Normal School, 66, Tang Shiquan; Education Institute, 75, Wang Weixian; Private Xichang School, 35, Wang Weixian; Songjiang Middle School, 32, Xu Xienong; Fisheries School, 71, He Liangxin; Yixing Middle School, 32, Liu Pingfan.

Jiangbei District: Yangzhou Middle School, 105, Zhu Lianfang; Xuzhou Middle School, 50, Yu Bin; Rugao Normal School, 35, Wang Ke; Donghai Normal School, 64, Huang Jinwen; Tongxue Academy, 65, Xu Wanlan; Nantong Middle School, 44, Zhou Chaofan; Huaiyin Normal School, 35, Su Jun; Huaian Middle School, 29, Wang Rong; Huaiyin Agriculture School, 70, Su Jun.

Field Exercise: Today's field exercise was originally scheduled to be held in Zhaze, but it was decided to change it to Laoshantou outside the East Gate due to the inconvenience of traveling back and forth over the sketch. The entire team is divided into North and South armies, with one based on the south side of the mountain and the other based on the north side. One is mainly defending and the other is mainly attacking, practicing encounter battles, reconnaissance actions, and occupying positions.

A Glimpse of the Campsite: The campsite is divided into North and South zones. The Jiangnan camp is located in the provincial stadium, with a total of fourteen schools, including Nanjing Middle School, which has the largest number of people, with eight bell-shaped tents and twelve house-shaped tents, which are neat and impressive. The interior of the tents is clean, and the students' discipline is particularly good. Other schools, such as Zhenjiang Normal School and Shangzhong, are also very neatly arranged. The camp gate of Zhenjiang Normal School is more unique than other schools. The Jiangbei district is located in the county stadium, with a total of nine schools, including Yangzhou Middle School, camped on the east and west ends of the field. Nantong Academy is also there, and the academy's medical rescue team also came to Zhenjiang with the team, bringing a rescue vehicle and rescue supplies. The entire team wears white clothes and white hats, with red cross badges on their chests, and those who do not know the situation almost suspect that a large number of doctors have been invited.

Various Countries' Indemnity Funds and Educational and Cultural Undertakings (2)

2. The Maturity Period of the Returned Funds

In the sixth year of the Republic of China, China proposed to the Allied Powers to postpone the payment of indemnities. For the sake of enhancing the friendly relations and cultural ties between the two countries, Chinese and American figures further advocated that the US government should return all the remaining portions of the US indemnity funds. After this movement occurred, it was greatly supported by the political and academic circles in the United States. People like Senator Lodge, Representative Porter, Director of the Eastern Bureau of the State Department Marmary, Professor Monroe of Columbia University, and Miss Vautier in China all did their best. In the tenth year of the Republic of China, Ambassador Shi Zhaoji formally contacted the US side. Just as things were about to succeed, both the upper and lower houses of Congress were closed, and the matter was put on hold. It was not until the thirteenth year that the two houses of the US Congress passed the continuation of the return of the remaining portion of the indemnity funds to China, and expressed the hope that this fund would be used to develop China's educational and cultural undertakings. China was grateful for the great kindness of the United States and gladly accepted it.

3. The US Continues to Return the Funds

There was no formal exchange of notes between China and the United States regarding the return of the indemnity funds. The US Secretary of State only sent a note to the Chinese Ambassador to the United States on June 14th of the thirteenth year of the Republic of China (1924), stating that the US upper and lower houses of Congress had passed this fund return bill and it had been approved by the US President. The Foreign Ministry of the Northern Government of China then sent a telegram in the name of the President to express its gratitude. The return of the funds was thus a great success.

4. Total Amount of Returned Funds

The total amount of the US indemnity funds returned was 6,137,552.90 US dollars in principal and 6,407,885.77 US dollars in interest, totaling 12,545,438.67 US dollars.

5. The Amount Allocated to Educational and Cultural Undertakings

The uses of the US indemnity funds are divided into (1) developing scientific knowledge and the application of this knowledge to China's circumstances, with the aim of promoting technical education, scientific research, experimentation and demonstration, and the training of scientific teaching methods; and (2) promoting cultural undertakings of a permanent nature, such as libraries. Each year, a portion of the returned funds is allocated to a permanent fund, and the remainder is used for educational and cultural undertakings as follows: (1) scientific professorships; (2) scientific research professorships; (3) scientific research grants and scholarships; (4) the Scientific Education Advisory Committee, later changed to the Editorial Committee; (5) the Social Investigation Institute; (6) the National Peiping Library; (7) the Jing Sheng Biological Investigation Institute; (8) subsidies to the China Science Society Geological Survey, the Chinese Vocational Education Society, and universities such as Datong, Nankai, Lingnan, Fudan, Zhonghua, Jinling, etc., the Wenhua Library, the Palace Museum, the Industrial Practice Society, the National Language Unification Preparatory Committee, the Chinese Education Improvement Society, the Chinese Civilian Education Promotion Association, the Chinese Geographical Society, and the Chinese United Mulberry Improvement Association, etc. The exact amount used for educational and cultural undertakings in each year was 1,826,822.12 national currency yuan in the fourteenth year, 1,610,294.05 in the fifteenth year, 1,463,310.24 in the sixteenth year, 1,732,708.12 in the seventeenth year, 1,931,948.27 in the eighteenth year, and 1,740,700.62 in the nineteenth year. After the twentieth year, the data has not been investigated.

6. The Organization of the Board of Directors

Regarding the US indemnity funds, the board of directors is named the China Educational and Cultural Foundation Board of Directors, and is organized with fifteen directors, with China accounting for two-thirds and the United States accounting for one-third. The first time, they were appointed by the Chinese government. After that, each time there was a vacancy, the board of directors elected a replacement to be reported to the government for record. The term of office for the first time was determined by the board of directors by drawing lots at the third annual meeting, with the exception of three people who would serve another year. The remaining three people each would serve two, three, and four years. After that, the term would be five years. Their powers are based on the US Secretary of State's note and the Chinese Ambassador to the United States' reply, to preserve the US portion of the returned indemnity funds and use these funds to promote China's educational and cultural undertakings.

Ministry of Education Interpretation: Qualifications of Rural Normal School and Vocational School Graduates

The Ministry of Education, through the Hunan Provincial Department of Education, forwarded a request from the Yiyang County Education Bureau for an interpretation of the qualifications of rural normal school graduates and vocational school graduates (stating that according to the primary school regulations, those who graduated from a simplified normal school for two years or more and have served as primary school teachers for two years or more may be exempted from examinations and assessments, but those who graduated from a three-year rural normal school and have served for only one and a half years have only half a year less experience, but one year more academic qualifications, and according to the reasons given by these students, the practical results in school can offset this half-year of experience, and there is no conflict with the law, and they ask to be allowed to review their resumes. Furthermore, various vocational school graduates, based on the length of their studies, have exceeded the old-system middle school or simplified normal school, and their studies are also proficient in several subjects, and they are indeed qualified to serve as specialist teachers, and they have now reported for resume review one after another, but according to the primary school regulations and the county's review methods, there are no regulations for this qualification, and it is not known how it should be compared with the old-system of senior high school, or whether they should be allowed to review their qualifications. Please give instructions.) The ministry then instructed the department stating that it is said that the service period of graduates from the three-year rural normal school is one and a half years, which is half a year less than the experience stipulated in Article 78, Section 2 of the Primary School Regulations, but the academic qualification is one year more. The two offset each other and there is no discrepancy, and they should be allowed to review their resumes. As for the graduates of various vocational schools, whose qualifications are equivalent to those of the old-system middle school, they can also be allowed to review their resumes in accordance with the provisions of Article 78, Section 1 of the Primary School Regulations. However, vocational school graduates are all specializing in a certain subject, and should be allowed to serve as specialist teachers. Please take note immediately.

Ministry of Education Interpretation: Qualifications of Rural Normal School Special Course Graduates

The Ministry of Education, based on a report from the Jiangsu Department of Education, forwarded a request from the Kunshan County Education Bureau for the verification of the qualifications of the Kunshan, Jiading, and Qingpu counties' rural normal school special course graduates, and issued an instruction interpreting that, after investigating the ministry's instructions on the Huang Jiabai's request for interpretation of the rural normal school special course graduate's admission qualifications, the so-called "(otherwise, it should be judged based on the admission qualifications and the length of study)" refers to the admission qualifications and length of study stipulated by a certain rural normal school special course, and does not refer to the admission qualifications of each individual student. The logic is very clear. The department's interpretation of the admission qualifications of each individual student is a misunderstanding. If the admission qualifications stipulated by the Kunshan, Jiading, and Qingpu counties' rural normal school special course are junior high school graduates, and the length of study is two years, then the qualifications of the graduates of the school should be equivalent to two years of senior high school normal school, and there should be no difference due to the admission qualifications of each individual. Please take note immediately.

Recent Situation of Xiamen University's Finances: Chen Jiageng Still Remits 6,000 Yuan Per Month

(Xiamen Correspondent) Xiamen University was founded by overseas Chinese Chen Jiageng. It began in the tenth year of the Republic of China and has been around for fourteen years. Chen has used more than four million yuan. Recently, the economy in various places has been sluggish, especially in the Nanyang rubber tree and production industries. Therefore, Chen Jiageng's company has closed down and is being liquidated. Xiamen University's finances have been reduced repeatedly since Chen's business declined. The monthly expenses are about 20,000 yuan. On the revenue side, Chen Jiageng's main company in Singapore still remits 6,000 yuan per month, the central government subsidizes 5,000 yuan per month, and the Fujian Provincial Government subsidizes 5,000 yuan per month. These three items can get 16,000 yuan per month. If tuition income increases, it can offset it. Recently, since Song Ziwen left the Ministry of Finance, the central government has only been able to get half the amount, or 2,500 yuan per month. Therefore, if tuition income is low, it will not be enough. According to President Lin Wenqing, Jimei School was founded in the first year of the Republic of China, and Xiamen University was founded in the tenth year of the Republic of China. They have both been maintained for more than ten or twenty years by Chen Jiageng's personal efforts, using more than 10 million yuan. Last year, the school's finances had problems. Xiamen locals were asked to donate and organize the Xiamen University Cultural Promotion Association. With the support of all sectors of society, it only raised 6,000 yuan in four months. Last year, in August, I went to Nanyang on business and only raised 6,000 yuan, etc.

Chinese Medical Association Holds Second Annual Meeting in Beijing

(Nanjing, 2nd) More than 200 members of the Chinese Medical Association's Second Annual Meeting visited the Sun Yat-sen Mausoleum at 7:00 AM on the 2nd. The opening ceremony was held at the Lishi Society at 9:00 AM, with more than 400 members and guests in attendance. Chairman Qi Shounan gave a speech, briefly stating that the association was established in the fourth year of the Republic of China and has a history of twenty years. It has grown from 36 members to more than 1,700 members, and he detailed three points: (1) scientific medicine, (2) physician education, and (3) physician investigation and improvement. Next, Chu Minyi, the representative of the Executive Yuan, gave a speech, briefly stating that medicine must be studied openly and thoroughly, adopting scientific methods. There should be no distinctions based on names such as Chinese medicine, Western medicine, or German medicine. One should focus on the whole country, the whole world, and all of humanity. Next, Wang Shijie gave a speech, briefly stating that China has had contact with European and Western culture for hundreds of years, but scientific medicine has still not developed. There are several reasons for this: one is the number of medical talents, one is the ethics of medicine, three is the general public's inability to afford medicine, and four is the low level of general education. He hoped that everyone would contribute more to the first three points in order to promote scientific medicine. Next, Liu Ruiheng gave a speech, briefly stating that the papers at this conference are very valuable. They are not words of ideal plans and criticisms, but are all based on science, and the authors are all well-known people in the country, which is a special feature. He hoped that everyone would visit the Health Department's Health Experimental Office and the Central Hospital and give more guidance. Then, Chairman and Acting President Niu Huisheng read a speech, reporting on the association's affairs in great detail. The meeting adjourned for a photo at 11:00 AM. All members then opened an administrative meeting. Sectional meetings, reports, and papers were held at 2:00 PM.

Jiangxi Education Department Holds Primary School Cleanliness Competition

(Nanchang Correspondent) In order to implement health education and promote schools' concern for cleanliness and hygiene, the Jiangxi Education Department held a provincial capital primary school cleanliness competition last month. Personnel were dispatched to various schools to conduct on-site inspections. It is reported that the inspection results showed that Bao Ling Girls' Middle School Affiliated Elementary School and Yu Zhang Affiliated Elementary School scored above 80 points, Tingrunmen Elementary School and eight other schools scored above 70 points, and Dacheng Elementary School and fifteen other schools scored above 60 points. The remaining schools scored below 60 points, with Mingde Girls' School and Qizhi Poor Children's School having the best results. In addition to rewarding and punishing according to the competition rules, in order to make all schools pay special attention to cleanliness and hygiene, twenty-four points for attention were set and strictly ordered all schools to comply and report. The points for attention are summarized as follows: (1) A major cleaning should be carried out, (2) a cleanliness inspection team should be organized, (3) the principal and teachers should set an example, (4) drainage ditches should be provided, (5) all rooms should be explored for light and ventilation, (6) more spittoons should be placed, (7) kitchens and toilets should be separated, (8) kitchen utensils should be washed with caustic soda regularly, etc., twenty-four points.

Two New Books on Reviving National Culture

The May Fourth Movement was the central social turning point in modern Chinese history, its greatness akin to the Renaissance in Western Europe. Even now, one can imagine the fiery, active revolutionary sentiments of the youth of that time. Recently, Chen Duanzhi, based on a new historical perspective and relying on firsthand experiences, has written "A Historical Evaluation of the May Fourth Movement," analyzing the causes and consequences of the movement from multiple angles. He also explores the trend of national cultural revival and the path of revolutionary consciousness construction from various aspects. Notably, the book includes writings by Cai Jiemin, a leader of the movement, which are particularly valuable. Chen's other book, "Lectures on Modern Social Science," is also a groundbreaking standard work on social science. It includes annotations for eighty famous Chinese and foreign social science works. Anyone who wants to understand the principles of modern social science and the path of social science changes must read it. This book is especially suitable for use as a textbook in universities. The former has already been printed, and the latter was published last week, priced at one dollar and twenty cents. It is available at major bookstores such as Shenghuo, Kaiming, and Xiandai.

Free Talk

How to Transcend Crisis

— Xu Maoyong

If there is a true (factual) crisis, and it (intensifies) and becomes (acute), then what? The answer to this question is also easy; it is still the same old thing, but it is not only unfavorable to both sides but downright unfavorable to all parties. A certain monk asked (seeking the Way): (What about taking three steps forward?) The answer was: (Bumping your head). (What about taking three steps back?) (Falling a thousand feet). (What about not advancing or retreating?) (Instant death). Then what should one do?!…

The above is the last paragraph of Mr. Wu's article (Crisis). (What should one do?) The text ends there. Who can answer this question?

Before there is a perfect answer, I can offer my opinion. But I will not express my opinion in my own words, because there are ready-made words that can be used. These words appeared in (Free Talk) some time ago, contained in a folk song from Anhui introduced by Mr. Ruizhi: The first half of that folk song says:

(Big stars in the sky face small stars, an eighteen-year-old girl has been looking for her lover until now, not knowing how many dark nights she has walked through, nor how much fear and fright she has suffered. Standing, she fears being seen; lying down, she fears being bitten by mosquitoes. Walking to the front village, the dogs bark; walking to the back village, the tigers growl.) This is indeed what is called (unfavorable to all parties). (Then what should one do?) But the end says:

(One can only summon up the courage and look forward, calling out to her lover with both tenderness and reproach.)

(One can only summon up the courage and look forward). This is also my opinion.

Mr. Wu also mentioned Caesar in his article. One of his stories can serve as a footnote to this saying:

After the Roman Senate issued an order prohibiting Caesar from returning to Rome, Caesar, who was in Gaul, recklessly raised an army in rebellion. But when he reached the Rubicon River, which was between Gaul and Rome, he could not help but hesitate: Should he cross the river? That would be defying the Senate's order and would inevitably lead to rebellion, but Pompey's power was strong, and the outcome was uncertain. Should he return to Gaul? That would be surrendering to the Senate's order, which he was unwilling to do. Moreover, he would inevitably be annihilated by them in the future…

(What should one do?) As a result of much deliberation, Caesar finally shouted Alea Zacta est! (Let the die be cast!) and crossed the river.

If one does not summon up the courage to move forward, what else can one do? Run crookedly across the desert like an ostrich, or hide one's head in one's wings? But they are often more easily captured by hunters.

In the end, there is only the way back. But if there is a stable road to retreat behind, then what kind of crisis is it!

Half a Day's Work

— Li Huiying

(Jingzhen, aren't you getting up yet? It's almost seven o'clock.)

Hearing my mother's shout from the main room, I woke up from my dream. The sun was already shining on the windowsill. I don't know why, but for the past two years, I have always lacked enthusiasm for going to school in the morning. It's not like before, when I considered this matter more important than eating, fearing that I would be reprimanded by the teacher if I was late. Now, it's completely different. Going to school and attending classes is just an ordinary thing for me; I'm simply going through the motions. According to my own wishes, I would have long stopped going to school to receive this education as a slave of a conquered nation. I would rather stay at home and do nothing. But after thinking about it carefully, since I cannot escape the current harsh environment, and since I have the opportunity to go out and study, to go and walk around, then instead of simply wasting my days at home, it is better to go to school. By doing so, I can also gain a better understanding of how education as a slave of a conquered nation differs from education in the past, and what direction the development of education as a slave of a conquered nation will take in the future. Therefore, for the past two years, I have remained a student in name only. To be honest, I have never once seriously looked at my homework. Perhaps this is why I get up so late in the morning.

Looking up at the small clock on the table next to me, it was once smashed by a Japanese soldier who broke in to inspect. Later, a new piece of glass was put on it. The clock face clearly indicates that it is only five minutes to seven o'clock. Yes, it's not early; it's time for me to get up.

(Ah! I'm getting up, Mother.)

Answering my mother's call, I turned over and got out of bed. While getting dressed, I suddenly remembered what the training director reported yesterday. He wanted all the students to arrive at school promptly at 7:30 this morning. Yes, as he said, today is September 15th, the anniversary of the first week of the (New Country) being recognized by Japan. There will be a grand celebration. Time has passed unnoticed for five minutes. It's exactly seven o'clock. I cannot afford to delay any longer. I hurriedly washed my face, ate breakfast, and then said goodbye to my mother: (Mother, I'm leaving.)

The road was as peaceful as usual, except that every household had a new national flag hanging at the door, fluttering in the September morning breeze. Everywhere on the walls, there was no shortage of colorful paper slogans. Because the colors were so dazzling, some passersby used their literacy skills to stop and read them aloud.

(Celebrating the first anniversary of the recognition of the New Country.)

(Celebrating the recognition, we thank our friendly neighbors for their great kindness.)

(Long live the Great Japanese Empire.)

(Long live the Great Manchurian Empire.)

(Suppress bandits, pacify the people, and implement benevolent rule.)

I had already read through them twice as I heard others reciting them. I planned to read them again to see if there were any other slogans. Finally, I saw a newly posted large advertisement on another wall, clearly showing two lines of text in black ink:

(Commemorating the two-year anniversary of September 18th.)

(Commemorating the one-year anniversary of September 15th.)

Hakka Love Songs

— Qiutao

(1) Not afraid of being beaten, not worried about being scolded, slipping out the back door when beaten at the front door; even if the skin is bruised and the tendons are not broken, I won't give up on my lover until I die!

(2) Daring to release doves, daring to put on bells, daring to walk on the road with my lover; if anyone dares to spread rumors of adultery, I'll take the lawsuit to Nanjing City.

(3) Not afraid of death, not afraid of life, not afraid of my husband's broken ankles; even if the ankles are broken, leaving only toes, we will keep going as long as we both have our lives.

(Note) The word (唔) means the same as (不), or "not."

Farewell

— Wei Mang

We sat silently and forlornly by the window. Dusk had already crept into the room, and the courtyard was silent.

We were almost glad to have this dusk in the courtyard all to ourselves on this day. At the same time, we could not help but feel a deep sense of sadness in the silence of this dusk.

There were so many things we wanted to say to each other. We were a newly married couple. Looking at each other, tears filled our eyes. I reached out and held her hand tightly. In front of us were a quilt, a suitcase, and a net basket. I was almost crying!

These past few days, I have seen her forcing a smile, and the sadness in my heart is something that only those who have experienced it can understand. She would often walk into the next room with tears in her eyes during our private conversations. She did not let her emotions of parting be fully revealed in front of me. She was controlling herself. I had also told her not to worry about packing, that it was nothing to me, and that I could get it all done in an hour or two.

Unexpectedly, I went to the market in the afternoon, and when I came back, the net basket, suitcase, and quilt had all been arranged properly.

She had opened the suitcase for me to see, and all the clothes I needed to wear had been placed inside. There was also a handwritten list of clothes attached to the inside of the lid. All the books in the net basket were ones that I wanted to take with me, and the inkstone box had been polished brightly, with white cotton paper prepared inside. There were also several new pens with copper pen caps.

I don't need to describe the feelings I had when I later found a handkerchief that she often used in my pocket. At that moment, I could not help but feel sad.

My mother died early, and I have no sisters. Family was simply a cold memory for me in the past; my heart had never been warmed here. At that time, how could I have imagined that parting would be so painful for me today?

I said quietly:

(I will come back as soon as I have a vacation.) As soon as I said it, I knew it was a foolish thing to say, but unexpectedly, because of this foolish thing, she could not restrain her emotions after all, and she cried on my shoulder.

I kissed her, but I couldn't find a smarter word to comfort her!

On Translation (Continued)

— Dun

Then what if there are difficulties? Either translate the original text and consult the dictionary, or better yet, use a consultant, or even better, a foreign engineer! There is no other way. In scholarship, there is no room for pretense, no royal road, and no room for trickery! 2. Oral translation is better than written translation, and collaborative translation is better than individual translation. Except for literary works that require a unique understanding, such as poetry, where one feels that only oneself can translate it, it is easier for two or three people (too many people can be inconvenient) with common interests to study and discuss together, and they can have more interest, less effort, and more success. But it also requires calmness and tranquility; no quarreling allowed! No fighting allowed! Although it is admirable to bear the burden alone and endure the loneliness, it is ultimately unnecessary! There is also a small experience to share with book translators, namely that translating is sometimes not troublesome, but copying a huge work is felt to be a heavy task. The simple method is to have someone else copy it after revising it.

Yan Jidao's theory of translation has three principles: fidelity, expressiveness, and elegance. These secretly align with the three principles of art: truth, goodness, and beauty. They can be taken as a model. Fidelity means truthfulness, expressiveness means clarity, and elegance means beauty. Now when we look at the Tang dynasty translations of Buddhist scriptures, especially the treatises and verses, we cannot help but be amazed at the profoundness of the ancients. In terms of reasoning, if one is slightly familiar with that kind of grammar, one feels that not a single word is moved, added, or subtracted. Luther and Melanchthon co-translated the Greek Bible, and the hardship of their work was such that they often translated only three lines in four days, but this established the foundation of the German language. The (Mandarin) translation of the Old and New Testaments is also a masterpiece. Generally speaking, after fidelity and expressiveness are achieved, a style naturally emerges, opening up a new literary form, which is to be expected. Perhaps asking the ancients to translate the Buddhist scriptures into another, more accessible and easier-to-understand literary form, so that ordinary people can easily understand them, and feel that they are (pleasing to the eye) is impossible. Fidelity can be achieved through effort, but expressiveness requires considerable talent. A's translation is inexpressive, but B's translation is expressive. There is a great difference in skill. Elegance can only be relied on heaven; it cannot be deliberately created. However, since there is already a style, it will naturally take on a certain form. Therefore, I have copied out the eight conditions of Master Yanzong:

In order to translate well, one must have eight preparations and ten rules:

1. Sincerely receive the Dharma, with the aim of benefiting others.

2. Before entering the battlefield, first secure the foundation of precepts.

3. Be proficient in the Three Treasures of the scriptures and penetrate the five vehicles of meaning.

4. Have broad knowledge of literature and history, and be skilled in embellishing classical phrases, but not clumsy.

5. Have a broad and tolerant mind, be open-minded and inclusive, and not be fond of clinging to one's own views.

6. Be immersed in Taoist arts and indifferent to fame and wealth, and not seek to show off.

7. Know Sanskrit and not abandon that learning.

8. Be familiar with Cang Jie and Ya, and be roughly familiar with seal script and official script, so as not to be ignorant of this writing.

In the past, in prosperous times, translation was regarded as an extremely noble and great undertaking, and translators were all (masters). This work was connected to religion, and was felt to be related to body, mind, and life, so although it was very hard, the results were particularly good. There are few typos in Buddhist scriptures, probably for this reason. Today, people translate Western works, but lack this kind of faith. Although some people use this to make a living, their aim is to sell books, which is no different from doing business. In business, all that matters is variety and quick delivery. They don't care about the essence, let alone the impact of a book after translation on the readers. It is even more amazing to see modern Westerners translating each other's works. Generally speaking, any important work that exists in country A will be translated in country B, so translating without the author's permission is considered theft. There are as many as forty translations of Faust in English, and even the Japanese have translated the complete works of literary figures such as Tolstoy and Shakespeare, which truly shames us!

Is there anyone who truly feels that they are shouldering the mission of introducing Western culture and solemnly regard translation as a lifelong work? We need such (masters)! (End)

No sun, no rain, spring often has these days. Women's bodies tremble: the mysterious street always carries fragrance.

X X X

Going Home

— Zang Kejia

|Random Notes from a Windowless Room, Part 2|

Suddenly, a whim came over me, and I felt that I wouldn't be happy unless I went home. My bizarre behavior was really prompted by a secret that I couldn't express, like sleepless nights and inexplicable heart palpitations that no one could understand. A sick heart is definitely not something that ordinary people can measure. If you told the truth about your heart, people would laugh at you. I understood this flavor, so whenever I wanted to do something very special, I always explained it to everyone with a different reason.

This time, the reason for returning home was to observe Qingming. I felt that this was enough to shut everyone up, because the reason seemed very legitimate. Isn't Qingming Festival a day for tomb sweeping? Moreover, land sales in the northern custom must be decided before this holiday. I am the sole owner of my family, which is well known to everyone.

(The countryside during Qingming Festival is really poetic!) Everyone said, and this really revealed half of my heart.

After running all day, I felt dizzy. The excessive insomnia and the excitement of anticipating the joy of returning home made my face burn. When I returned to the windowless room in the evening, oh, there were already three guests who had filled this small room. I felt happy because these three people were all people I liked, all like-minded. The three of them lay on the bed board, and I stood by the table, talking, talking. The topic didn't have a fixed direction, but every sentence and every word flowed from the heart and had a true flavor. (Ten o'clock!) Everyone seemed a little surprised. They wanted to leave, and I saw them out the door.

(Can't the windowless room keep you anymore?)

(It can't keep me.) The people had already gone far.

I turned back to the main room to say goodbye. My aunt was a little surprised.

(Who were those three people in Western clothes?)

(Friends.)

(This small room has become glorious because of you. (Talking and laughing with learned people, and there are no uneducated people coming and going.) This room can be called a humble room.)

The train carried me away from the city. The morning light shone on the open fields, and the open fields were green and full of life. I took a deep breath, as if I were seeing the sun for the first time. My heart also felt lighter.

The journey of eighty li only took two hours by train, but I didn't take it. There was my reason for this, which I couldn't tell anyone. I took a small cart, letting it bump and jostle on the uneven ancient road, until my bones ached. I was happy like this. The wheat seedlings had not yet covered the crows, stretching green from my feet to the horizon. A scent of earth rolled into my nostrils from the cartwheels, which was a supreme enjoyment. A row of weeping willows on the long embankment stretched as far as the eye could see, yellow, and there were already spring crows calling to pedestrians. The village girls washing clothes in the thawed little river wanted to see people first and blushed themselves first. Some naked children were busy building fish weirs, happily clapping their bare legs. I wanted to jump down and join in. I was born in the countryside, and this life is a true reflection of my childhood.

From afar, I saw the mountains of my hometown, and my heart used the mountains to measure the distance to my hometown. When I arrived home, it was already dusk, and there were many children flying kites in the evening breeze.

Under the small lamp, a group of people gathered to tell stories, and my heart was at peace. However, they told even more shocking real stories, giving me more evidence of the rural bankruptcy that I already knew. At night, I wanted to sleep, but I didn't dare to. I connected my heart and ears, and lay on my pillow listening to the movement of the dogs!

Securities and Bond Market Climbs to New Heights

All Bonds Reach New High Prices

Yesterday, the Shanghai Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange suddenly saw a sharp rise in the market. Although the market price was high, buyers did not dislike the high price. Oil Market

Coal Oil Market Prices Surge by 80 Cents

Coal oil prices have slightly increased since the 2nd of this month due to taxes. New brand coal oil (such as Happiness, Monk Hat, and Eagle brands) has increased by 80 cents, from the original price of $6.40 per pair (two cans) to the current price of $7.20. Old brand coal oil (such as Red Star and Yuan Bao) has also increased by 80 cents, from the original price of $6.60 per pair (two cans) to a uniform price of $7.40. Gasoline is currently selling at 80 cents, a 10-cent increase, with wholesale at 70 cents. The above prices are for sales in this port; prices in other areas may vary slightly due to water transportation costs and other expenses, adding about 10 cents to the prices in this port. The price of white tung oil in Hanshi continues to rise.

[ 　　丨Fine Tung Oil Market Opened Before Yesterday丨 　　]

The price of white tung oil has suddenly risen continuously in recent days. According to details from Hankou, the source is too scarce. The price for sales to foreign firms has increased to $25. However, foreign firms in Hankou are not actively purchasing goods, and American firms are maintaining a very calm attitude. Although European firms have made some transactions, they are limited. The main reason for the price increase is the sudden scarcity of goods, which cannot meet demand. If there is a significant increase in foreign sales, the situation is unpredictable. According to Ying Hang's purchases, the price has already reached $20.34 per "zhi" and may increase by another 6 to 7 cents, while Xiang Tung has reached $21. Local firms in this port are very calm about this price increase because the spring sales have not been strong. Although there is talk of selling Zhejiang tung oil at $21 per "zhu," no deals have been made. The stagnant sales market cannot stimulate buyers' interest, even with rising prices. Based on the current market, unless there are large-scale foreign sales, the price is likely to stabilize at this level. The production volume of fine tung oil in recent years is significantly different from the past. Recently, local firms in this port opened purchases from Wan Xing Yu, Da You Heng, Ji Feng Heng, Ji Tai Heng, and other top-quality brands, totaling about 1,000 barrels. The price of the Wan brand is slightly below $30 per barrel, while the prices of the Da Ji and Liang Sheng brands are slightly lower as usual. However, the quantity is small, and sellers are hoarding the goods.

Silk and Tea

Ningzhou Tea Industry Shows Slight Vigor

Ningzhou in Jiangxi Province has historically been an important area for producing and selling black tea to foreign firms. During the peak of Russian sales, the annual export of black tea from this region reached over 100,000 boxes, surpassing the position of Qimen black tea. Since 1920, the production of Indian and Ceylon black tea has been exceptionally strong due to the warm climate. The Ningzhou tea sales in the major markets of England and Russia have been almost entirely taken over. In recent years, only Guangdong's Zhen Zhi Company and local firms have produced and sold 5,000 to 6,000 boxes in Shanghai. The tea industry in this region has been largely ignored. However, since British and Dutch tea merchants have repeatedly restricted production, the prices of Indian and Ceylon tea have recently increased by 30% to 40%. As a result, tea merchants are hopeful about the future of Ningzhou tea and are sending people to the mountains to purchase tea, making it much more active than in previous years.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Discourse on New Morality and (Old Morality) Ji Yun

The two words "(New)" and "(Old)" are naturally affirmed by comparing them with each other using time as the standard. Material objects with tangible bodies are particularly clearly expressed due to their temporal nature. For example, new clothes and old clothes, new houses and old houses, and even new people and old people, new countries and old countries, new China and old China, are all distinguished by the order of their creation and embryonic state. Even intangible and incorporeal things (abstract things) are distinguished as new or old based on the timing of their occurrence, such as new ideas and old ideas, new doctrines and old doctrines, none of which can escape the determination of time.

There are also things that are not subject to the constraints of time, that do not change their constant form or state. They remain the same after thousands of years as they were thousands of years ago. The scorching sun does not diminish its power over billions of spring and autumn seasons, and the bright moon does not diminish its brilliance over billions of spring and autumn seasons. Therefore, terms such as "new sun" and "old sun," "new moon" and "old moon" are merely materials for literary and ink play. There is no real distinction between new and old in form. Extending this principle, one can understand that any object, because of the tight organization between its molecules, will never be eroded by time and can always maintain its (newness).

(Morality) is a treasure for guiding human conduct and has its own value of existence. It maintains its dignity and, like the sun and moon, cannot be distinguished as new or old. We stubbornly use things that do not last as examples to distinguish between (new morality) and (old morality), which is unreasonable.

Thousands of years ago, people said, "(One must have sincerity and trustworthiness)," can people in the twentieth or even the hundredth century act deceitfully? Some of the past methods of self-cultivation and governance are considered obsolete, but once they are violated, one will be subject to centrifugal forces and environmental constraints. Therefore, morality is absolutely new, with no distinction between (new morality) and (old morality). Moreover, since it is called (old morality), I wonder where the (new morality) is. One can also ask, "(What is called new morality?)"

Those who are not deeply involved in the world and have weak wills misinterpret this issue, creating countless evils. I want to say in a literary way, "(The one who first made burial figures, will he have no descendants?)"

To put it another way, if new clothes are not yet made, one still wears the old ones; if a new house is not yet built, one still lives in the old one; if the new harvest has not yet come to the market, one still continues to eat old rice. By making such accommodations, at the very least, one will not suffer from cold, hunger, or starvation. If everyone can learn by analogy, society will be much more peaceful.

After Watching the Play Performed by Qingxin Girls' School Fang Zhi Zhong

Evaluation of (Black Bat) Performance

Although I had one semester of history with Qingxin Boys' School in the past, I have always found Qingxin Girls' School, which is close by, desirable but unreachable. Later, although close, they felt like distant neighbors, and I even had fewer chances to see them from afar. Yesterday, I learned that the school was performing a play directed by my old friend Mr. Ying Yunwei, and the thought of seeing it dominated my actions.

The tram sped through the chilly spring air, and soon I was at Kua Long Road. Kua Long Road has shed its former narrow, dirty appearance, revealing plump, clean arms. The two schools, boys' and girls', still stand opposite each other on either side of the road, but they are now more majestic than before. Reaching the gate of Qingxin Girls' School, several visitors were being stopped by the gatekeeper. I took out my name card and asked to see Director Ying. The gatekeeper courteously invited me in. Upon entering, a foreign atmosphere was evident. A patch

Cotton Yarn: April Yarn Discovered at a New Low Price in Ten Years

丨169 Yuan丨

The yarn market continued to fall, the situation being quite precarious. This was because manufacturers could not unite, and the amount of yarn delivered to the exchange was too great. A certain factory's long position was suppressed, and the accumulated amount was entirely liquidated, causing the market to loosen. General retail investors rushed to sell, causing the market to collapse. However, current yarn trading is relatively active. Affected by the unfavorable environment, market prices remain weak. Moreover, the old standard April yarn reached a new low in nearly ten years and broke through the 70 yuan mark.

At the opening of the futures yarn market, there was still no market for foreign cotton. There was a lack of sellers in the market, and the overall sentiment was very weak. Prices for each month fell by five, six, seven, or eight jiao (tenths of a yuan) to one yuan one jiao. In the afternoon, April yarn reached a new low in ten years, at 169 yuan, a further drop of one yuan one jiao. Distant months fell four, seven, or eight jiao. The total trading volume for the day was 26,250 bales. Of these, 1,300 bales of Dafu were sold, 900 bales of Minghua, 1,650 bales of Renfeng, 900 bales of Jinchang, and 950 bales of Gengfeng. 800 bales of Xincheng were bought, 900 bales of Hengchang, 600 bales of Shenji, 800 bales of Mingde, 850 bales of Yuanda, 400 bales of Chunjji Meiji, and 1,000 bales of Suilong. Finance: Foreign Exchange Still Chaotic

Banks Have Not Yet Fully Resumed Business

Yesterday, on the banking front, because foreign merchants were still in the period of closing their accounts, only Chinese merchants were open for business. Therefore, although there were no obstacles to transactions, the situation was still somewhat simplified. There was no change in the foreign exchange market. The morning and afternoon markets were both at 4%, and there was no increase in "hua tou" (commission charged by money shops). In terms of "chai piao" (discounted draft) transactions, the morning market transferred over 4.4 million, and new transactions were over 300,000. Afternoon market transactions were over 200,000. Transactions in the Small General Association were over 400,000. Banks did not receive payments from foreign merchants because they were not open. There was no news of receipts. Chinese banks received over 3 million in drafts, over 3 million in various secured tax payments and miscellaneous expenses, and 300,000 in warehouse releases. Money shops received over 41.1 million in foreign public bills, over 2.1 million in foreign "hua tou" payments, over 300,000 in remittances from various routes, 200,000-300,000 in cash receipts, over 600,000 in foreign pledges, over 1.4 million in banknote inflows and outflows, 200,000 in customer sources, and 350,000 in outflows. In addition, the total amount of exchanges in the Shanghai Clearing House on the 2nd was 8,388,201.85 silver dollars, including 4,724,614.28 silver dollars and 3,663,587.57 silver dollars in remittances.

Grain: Northern and Southern Rice Markets Show No Major Fluctuations

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, there were more than 40 sources (over 6,000 shi (a unit of volume)), with thick japonica rice being more abundant and late rice being slightly scarce, with only a dozen or so sources. The customer base was slightly less enthusiastic, and the sellers were all trying to do well, resulting in a tight situation. From the beginning of the market, the Northern Ocean guild took the lead in making advances, followed by the Southern Ocean guild, so the trend slightly shifted, and with limited arrivals, confidence stabilized. Sellers took the opportunity to raise prices, resulting in a tight situation. Unexpectedly, both the Northern and Southern Ocean guilds stopped, and only 1,405 packages were handled, and the purchase demand was difficult to loosen, which affected the market situation. Although sellers wanted to do well, they ultimately failed to reverse the situation, and all the good signs vanished. As a result, Qingjiao, Songsi, Xilian, and other varieties all showed a stable situation, and the market showed no upward or downward fluctuations. However, according to boatmen, it is currently the incense season, and they have a custom of traveling together to offer incense, so they have temporarily stopped transporting goods. In that case, according to this situation, the arrival volume in various ports will inevitably be scarce in the next few days. If sales can be strong, it will be optimistic. The overall trend of thick japonica rice in each guild was similar to the previous day. Du Yang tip and Yin Bian Yuan had no significant changes.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, 34 or 35 boats arrived from various ports downstream, and the sales of each guild were still good. The market for white japonica rice, Yang Du, Kejian, were steady, and the price of port-tip goods was tight by 3-5 fen due to scarcity. Early japonica rice was the same as yesterday, with no ups or downs. Bian Yuan and Yin Yuan were quite popular, and prices were stable.

Small Refined Rice Waiting for Price to Sell

Customers' Indica Rice Arrivals Already Scarce

Yesterday's customer indica rice market was characterized by scarce arrivals from Hunan and Jiangxi, and other routes also declined. Due to the previous standstill of local customers, market prices were low, and customer traders were uniformly looking outward. Production prices in Hunan and Jiangxi provinces were high, making it even more difficult to agree on deals. On the sales side, there were few customers coming to the market due to the recent Spring Festival holiday, and the local street was also looking outward. There were few transactions throughout the day, and the market was temporarily stagnant. Yesterday, the market handled 405 packages of Fuzhou entertainment Nanjing Jixiang rice, over 200 packages of various brown rice, and Wenzhou handled 400 packages of Wuhu rice. Local streets handled over 300 packages of Jixiang, late brown rice, indica rice, etc. The market was high-quality, with some added charges because the owners raised prices due to reduced arrivals and rising production prices. For example, Wuhu Jixiang rice and Nanjing indica rice both rose by several fen. The foreign rice in the hands of foreign merchants has already been settled with the trade. The 35,000 packages of small refined rice stored in Anli were also sold out at a price of 6 yuan 5 jiao. However, traders are optimistic and mostly hoarding it. A small amount is allocated to the Ningbo guild. Now that tariffs are in effect, future prices are uncertain. With little stock in Shanghai, hoarders are optimistic. Yesterday, the local street handled 500 packages of recycled small refined rice, still opening at 6 yuan 7 jiao 5 fen.

Soybeans Rise Again by Two or Three Fen

Yesterday's soybean market continued the momentum of the previous week and rose again by two or three fen. The reason is that the source is still not abundant, and the sales are continuous, and the confidence is turning firm. Yesterday, factories handled four vehicles of Bengbu beans, with a price of 2 yuan 5 jiao. They also handled three vehicles of Yingzhou beans, ranging from 2 yuan 6 jiao to 5 jiao 9 fen. Local streets purchased two vehicles of Feihe beans, with prices of 2 yuan 7 jiao 2 fen and 7 jiao. One vehicle of Yingzhou beans was also traded, with a price of 2 yuan 6 jiao 2 fen. More than 170 packages of Zhengyangguan beans were handled, with a price of 2 yuan 7 jiao 7 fen. There was also a vehicle of Zhengyang beans, with a price of 2 yuan 8 jiao, reportedly for export.
